Really lively place. Went there on a Saturday night.Right next to "off the hook" seafood restuarant and a liquor store. It has three pool tables, two dart machines. TVs on each corner of the bar area. For a dive bar,(according to my perspective and observation)it really spacious. The lighting is bright, which is a nice touch on the owners part. Really good crowd. It has a good balance of regulars and new visitors. You can tell its a tight knit group and know each other. The bartenders were britni and tawni. They were excellent in handling orders and customer service. I would go back again, because of warm reception  of the crowd and its interesting interaction.</review>

< review>
Decided after being seT for several years, to give this place a try again. Apparently in the last 8 years it has turned from a neighborhood bar into a bikini bar after 3pm. While there is nothing wrong with this, and the drinks are still reasonably priced and the pours aren't stingy, the clients are mostly young males. The bartenders-all females- cater to the males, and females, especially non-20 somethings are pretty much ignored--unless you are using the restroom. Then suddenly there's a scantily clad employee right there -making for a very uncomfortable experience. 20-30 yr old males will find this place perfect after 3pm.  Prior to 3pm, it is still a great neighborhood bar to get strong inexpensive drinks.</review>

< review>
Situated in downtown Sacramento, the Leland Stanford Mansion State Historic Park is a must-see California Historical Landmark that was constructed in 1856.

During a visit to this massive property, you‚Äôll see historic works of art, beautiful woodwork, 17-foot high ceilings, and period furniture. Guided tours of the property are available.< /review>

< text>
Beautiful mansion that was the office of the Governor during the Civil War.  More recently it was the second office of Schwarzenegger.  The grounds are kept vintage Victorian.  The entire mansion and grounds are operated by California State Parks. Walk up Tours available...check the State Parks website for hours.
I took these photos in the early morning.  The juxtaposed image of Victorian Sacramento against a 1960s high rise is beautiful.</text>

114073634912609673945< /userid>
<username>C Finigan</username><Time>1544758015944</Time>< Rate>
5< /Rate>
< review>
The Leland Stanford Mansion is just absolutely gorgeous. I was very enamored of the grand architecture. Some of the decorative elements are reproductions, however most are original to the mansion. Unfortunately, no photography is allowed inside the mansion, due to the California executive security detail. The mansion is used by the governor for hosting events involving visiting dignitaries, hence the censorship of photography. Regardless of this, I strongly recommend visiting this California treasure, for she is probably the sole surviving residence of one of California's big Railroad Four, Governor Leland Stanford. The tour is free to the public, and the mansion's history is absolutely unique.</review>

< user_id>
103110474612803128742<//user_id>
<Name>Casey Rafter</Name><time>1566244612840<//time>< rate>
5</rate>
< text>
My partner in crime and I have been to the *other* governor's mansion in town, but hadn't visited LSM yet. On Saturday, while celebrating our 11'th anniversary, we planned a visit to check out what this site was all about.
The lobby is packed with great info on the development and history of the mansion It's INCREDIBLE what changes the home, the property, and Sacramento has gone through over the last 100 years.
Our guide, Ryan, was so friendly and patient with the kids in our group. He had a very obvious passion for his job and for the history of the mansion and it's owners and residents over time. I feel like I learned so much about Sacramento simply from our short little visit to this beautiful home.
I am SO THIRSTY to sneak a peek at the rooms we're not allowed to enter. You won't see it all because there isn't photographic evidence to help restoration of certain parts of the home. DO NOT expect to take any photos during the tour (you can outside of the mansion) and make sure to hydrate first because there's no opportunity to drink while you're inside.
Very friendly docents, very informative and amazing tour, and it's an incredible part of Sacramento's history.<//text>

<user_id>115059493829360030989< /user_id><text>Took the kids to explore a park we haven't been to before since moving into to Modesto. We found this Modesto park much more pleasant than others. Definitely more well kept than other ones! What I do find odd about Modesto parks; no doors on the bathroom stalls. What is up with that! I also like to state a word of caution: The children's play area is much older with metal slides and NOT toddler proof. Parents will need to keep a closer eye on younger ones here. Still fun of course; the kids liked the tire swings the best. And the play area stands on sand so carefully choose your shoes. The play area is not the best place to go when the heat is very hot considering the metal will burn skin. A good plus, the trees are mature, providing lots of shade. My children also enjoyed running around the baseball fields, which are nicely kept. There is a large and covered picnic area as well with plenty of parking around it. The park is also a nice walking area.</text>< pictures>

< text>
On our way North to Oregon, we decided to stop by this sandwich shop, based on their reviews. When we arrived we were met by John, who went out of his way to make us feel welcome, as he explained the different menu items for us. He even came from around the counter to point out different specials on the menu board. They have different sandwich specials for each day of the week, which were a pretty good deal. The sandwiches were incredibly good!!! They have something they call 'silly sauce' which, with all the other ingredients and bread, tasted great! John also asked us about our trip and the big UO game we were going to see - Really nice guy!  On our way back from the game, we stopped by there again. The service we received from Steve and Sarah this time was just as good as it was on our first visit with John. Just off the freeway, we were in and out again in no time going to/from Oregon. Overall, great food, service, location and prices :)</text>

The disc golf course is over 3 miles long with multiple basket positions at each hole. We met 97 year old Don on the course, it was inspiring playing with him, he started at 92 and is really good. < review>
This park has helped me create many memorable moments. The ducks, geese, a  multitude of different birds have bred with a variety of birds creating a mix of over a dozen of different types of ducks, geese and other birds are SO unique and native ONLY to Waller Park. (Imbreeding HAS led to some vicious geese & some of the birds have been known to approach and nip/bite park-goers who fed or would feed them. Thankfully there is a NEW rule, NO FEEDING THE BIRDS. The park has repaired the pond fountains and refilled them. There's tons of community activities here, and now that it's being maintained better than EVER, it's a GREAT place to have outdoor parties or events. A nice family park, huge, with MULTIPLE bathrooms and playgrounds. A dog park and more. It's a beautiful area to spend some time just laying around.<//review>

< Text>
Waller Park is a very well taken care of park with a dog run, many ducks and different kinds if animals also and a friendly amount of squirrels. There's much to explore with many children's playgrounds and a small pond to see the ducks and geese swim. This is a very nice place to take pictures of plants and animals. The parks here are widely used and the dog run always has many dogs included inside. The park is a high rated park due to the fact that it is taken very well care of. The one downside to the park is that the majority of people here are not very friendly and so it is best to bring your own animal and/or family member so you have a better time and maybe there is a chance you might meet someone new, but they seem to be very antisocial.< /Text>
